ns-0 ns-subject page-Great_Recession rootpage-Great_Recession skin-vector action-view">\t\t<div id="mw-page-base" class="noprint"></div>\n\t\t<div id="mw-head-base" class="noprint"></div>\n\t\t<div id="content" class="mw-body" role="main">\n\t\t\t<a id="top"></a>\n\t\t\t<div id="siteNotice" class="mw-body-content"><!-- CentralNotice --></div><div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n</div>\n<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Great Recession</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">\xc2\xa0\xc2\xa0(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Late-2000s_recession&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Late-2000s recession">Late-2000s recession</a>)</span></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Early 21st-century global economic decline</div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the global economic downturn during the early 21st century. For background on financial market events dating from 2007, see <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%932008" title="Financial crisis of 2007\xe2\x80\x932008">Financial crisis of 2007\xe2\x80\x932008</a>.</div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>.</div>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:372px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GDP_Real_Growth.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/GDP_Real_Growth.svg/370px-GDP_Real_Growth.svg.png" width="370" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/GDP_Real_Growth.svg/555px-GDP_Real_Growth.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/GDP_Real_Growth.svg/740px-GDP_Real_Growth.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="940" data-file-height="415" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GDP_Real_Growth.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>World map showing <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(real)_growth_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by GDP (real) growth rate">real GDP growth rates</a> for 2009 (countries in brown were in recession.)</div></div></div>\n<p>The <b>Great Recession</b> was a period of general economic decline observed in world markets during the late 2000s and early 2010s. The scale and timing of the recession varied from country to country.<sup id="cite_ref-DPAD121912_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DPAD121912-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN011513_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN011513-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> In terms of overall impact, the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> concluded that it was the worst global recession since the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> in the 1930s.<sup id="cite_ref-New_IMF_Global_Recession_definition_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_IMF_Global_Recession_definition-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IMF_WEO_2009_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMF_WEO_2009-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The causes of the recession largely originated in the United States, particularly the real-estate market, though policies of other nations contributed as well. According to the U.S. <a href="/wiki/National_Bureau_of_Economic_Research" title="National Bureau of Economic Research">National Bureau of Economic Research</a> (the official arbiter of U.S. recessions) the recession, as experienced in that country, began in December 2007 and ended in June 2009, thus extending over 19 months.<sup id="cite_ref-nber.org_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nber.org-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The Great Recession was related to the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%932008" title="Financial crisis of 2007\xe2\x80\x932008">financial crisis of 2007 to 2008</a> and U.S. <a href="/wiki/Subprime_mortgage_crisis" title="Subprime mortgage crisis">subprime mortgage crisis</a> of 2007 to 2009. The Great Recession resulted in the scarcity of valuable assets in the market economy and the collapse of the financial sector (banks) in the world economy. The banks were then bailed out by the U.S. government.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The recession was not felt evenly around the world. Whereas most of the world\'s developed economies, particularly in North America and Europe, fell into a definitive recession, many of the newer developed economies suffered far less impact, particularly <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> and <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> whose economies grew substantially during this period.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminology">Terminology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Recession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Terminology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Two <a href="/wiki/Word_sense" title="Word sense">senses</a> of the word "[recession]" exist: a less precise sense, referring broadly to "a period of reduced economic activity";<sup id="cite_ref-Merriam-Webster_recession_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Merriam-Webster_recession-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> and the academic sense used most often in <a href="/wiki/Economics" title="Economics">economics</a>, which is <a href="/wiki/Operational_definition" title="Operational definition">defined operationally</a>, referring specifically to the <a href="/wiki/Inflection_point" title="Inflection point">contraction phase</a> of a <a href="/wiki/Business_cycle" title="Business cycle">business cycle</a>, with two or more consecutive quarters of <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a> contraction. Under the academic definition, the recession ended in the United States in June or July 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> In the broader, lay sense of the word however, many people use the term to refer to ongoing hardship (in the same way that the term "<a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>" is also popularly used).<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Recession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="vertical-navbox nowraplinks" style="float:right;clear:right;width:22.0em;margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em;background:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;padding:0.2em;border-spacing:0.4em 0;text-align:center;line-height:1.4em;font-size:88%;width:auto; clear:none; border-collapse:collapse;"><tbody><tr><th style="padding:0.2em 0.4em 0.2em;font-size:145%;line-height:1.2em;background:#f0f0f0; border-bottom:1px #ccc solid; font-size:120%;"><a class="mw-selflink selflink">Great Recession</a></th></tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em;text-align:left">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Great_Recession_in_Africa" title="Great Recession in Africa">Africa</a></li>\n<li><a
