close; -webkit-column-width: close; column-width: close; list-style-type: lower-alpha;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-Excluded_countries-128"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Excluded_countries_128-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">105 out of the 206 <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states" title="List of sovereign states">sovereign countries</a> in the World, did not publish any quarterly GDP data for the 2006&#x2011;2013 period. The following 21 countries were also excluded from the table, due to only publishing unadjusted quarterly real GDP figures with no seasonal adjustment: <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">Guatemala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Macao" class="mw-redirect" title="Macao">Macao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_territories" title="Palestinian territories">Palestine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-qoq(-4)-129"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-qoq(-4)_129-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-qoq(-4)_129-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Only seasonally adjusted <a href="/wiki/Quarter_on_quarter" title="Quarter on quarter">qoq</a>-data can be used to accurately determine recession periods. When quarterly change is calculated by comparing quarters with the same quarter of last year, this results only in an aggregated -often delayed- indication, because of being a product of all quarterly changes taking place since the same quarter last year. Currently there is no seasonal adjusted qoq-data available for Greece and Macedonia, which is why the table display the recession intervals for these two countries only based upon the alternative indicative data format.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Bolivia-133"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Bolivia_133-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Bolivia had as of January 2014 only published seasonally adjusted real GDP data until Q1-2010, with the statistics office still to publish data for 2010-13.<sup id="cite_ref-Bolivian_s.a._real_GDP_1999-2010Q1_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bolivian_s.a._real_GDP_1999-2010Q1-132">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-El_Salvador-142"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-El_Salvador_142-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to the methodology note for the quarterly GDP of El Salvador, this data series include seasonally adjustments.<sup id="cite_ref-Methodology_note_for_the_quarterly_GDP_of_El_Salvador_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Methodology_note_for_the_quarterly_GDP_of_El_Salvador-141">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-G20-144"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-G20_144-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The G20-zone represents 85% of all <a href="/wiki/Gross_world_product" title="Gross world product">GWP</a>, and comprise 19 member states (incl. UK, France, Germany and Italy) along with the EU Commission as the 20th member, who represents the remaining 24 EU member states in the forum.<sup id="cite_ref-g20members_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-g20members-143">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Kazakhstan-148"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Kazakhstan_148-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Kazakhstan had as of January 2014 only published seasonally adjusted real GDP data until Q4-2009, with the statistics office still to publish data for 2010-13.<sup id="cite_ref-Kazakhstani_s.a._real_GDP_1994-2009_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kazakhstani_s.a._real_GDP_1994-2009-147">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Moldova-153"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Moldova_153-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Moldova had as of January 2014 only published seasonally adjusted real GDP data until Q4-2010, with the statistics office still to publish data for 2011-13.<sup id="cite_ref-Moldova_s.a._real_GDP_1995-2010_152-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moldova_s.a._real_GDP_1995-2010-152">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n</ol></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Country_specific_details_about_recession_timelines">Country specific details about recession timelines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Recession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Country specific details about recession timelines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Iceland fell into an economic depression in 2008 following the collapse of its banking system (<i>see <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%932011_Icelandic_financial_crisis" title="2008\xe2\x80\x932011 Icelandic financial crisis">2008\xe2\x80\x932011 Icelandic financial crisis</a></i>). By mid-2012 Iceland is regarded as one of Europe\'s recovery success stories largely as a result of a currency devaluation that has effectively reduced wages by 50%--making exports more competitive.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The following countries had a recession already starting in the first quarter of 2008: Latvia,<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> Ireland,<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> New Zealand,<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> and Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-stats.oecd.org_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats.oecd.org-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The following countries/territories had a recession starting in the second quarter of 2008: Japan,<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> Hong Kong,<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>  Singapore,<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> Italy,<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> Turkey,<sup id="cite_ref-stats.oecd.org_18-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats.oecd.org-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Germany,<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> United Kingdom,<sup id="cite_ref-stats.oecd.org_18-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats.oecd.org-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> the Eurozone,<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> the European Union,<sup id="cite_ref-stats.oecd.org_18-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats.oecd.org-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> and OECD.<sup id="cite_ref-stats.oecd.org_18-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats.oecd.org-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The following countries/territories had a recession starting in the third quarter of 2008: United States,<sup id="cite_ref-stats.oecd.org_18-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats.oecd.org-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Spain,<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> and Taiwan.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The following countries/territories had a recession starting in the fourth quarter of 2008: Switzerland.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>South Korea "miraculously" avoided recession with GDP returning positive at a 0.1% expansion in the first quarter of 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Of the seven largest economies in the world by GDP, only China avoided a recession in 2008. In the year to the third quarter of 2008 China grew by 9%. Until recently Chinese officials considered 8% GDP growth to be required simply to create enough jobs for rural people moving to urban centres.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> This figure may more accurately be considered to be 5\xe2\x80\x937% now that the main growth in working population is receding.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Ukraine went into technical depression in January 2009 with a GDP growth of \xe2\x88\x9220%, when comparing on a monthly basis with the GDP level in January 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> Overall the Ukrainian real GDP fell 14.8% when comparing the entire part of 2009 with 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> When measured quarter-on-quarter by changes of seasonally adjusted real GDP, Ukraine was more precisely in recession/depression throughout the four quarters from Q2-2008 until Q1-2009 (with respective qoq-changes of: -0.1%, -0.5%, -9.3%, -10.3%), and the two quarters from Q3-2012 until Q4-2012 (with respective qoq-changes of: -1.5% and -0.8%).<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Japan was in recovery in the middle of the decade 2000s but slipped back into recession and deflation in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> The recession in Japan intensified in the fourth quarter of 2008 with a GDP growth of \xe2\x88\x9212.7%,<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> and deepened further in the first quarter of 2009 with a GDP growth of \xe2\x88\x9215.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_instability_related_to_the_economic_crisis">Political instability related to the economic crisis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Recession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Political instability related to the economic crisis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>On February 26, 2009, an Economic Intelligence Briefing was added to the <a href="/wiki/President%27s_Daily_Brief" title="President&#39;s Daily Brief">daily intelligence briefings</a> prepared for the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a>. This addition reflects the assessment of U.S. intelligence agencies that the global financial crisis presents a serious threat to international stability.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Movimiento_15M_valencia_20-05-2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Movimiento_15M_valencia_20-05-2011.jpg/220px-Movimiento_15M_valencia_20-05-2011.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Movimiento_15M_valencia_20-05-2011.jpg/330px-Movimiento_15M_valencia_20-05-2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Movimiento_15M_valencia_20-05-2011.jpg/440px-Movimiento_15M_valencia_20-05-2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="667" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Movimiento_15M_valencia_20-05-2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Anti-austerity_movement_in_Spain" title="Anti-austerity movement in Spain">anti-austerity movement in Spain</a>, May 2011</div></div></div>\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/Business_Week" class="mw-redirect" title="Business Week">Business Week</a></i> stated in March 2009 that global political instability is rising fast because of the global financial crisis and is creating new challenges that need managing.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> The Associated Press reported in March 2009 that: United States "Director of National Intelligence Dennis Blair has said the economic weakness could lead to political instability in many developing nations."<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> Even some developed countries are seeing political instability.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC1_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC1-198">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> NPR reports that David Gordon, a former intelligence officer who now leads research at the <a href="/wiki/Eurasia_Group" title="Eurasia Group">Eurasia Group</a>, said: "Many, if not most, of the big countries out there have room to accommodate economic downturns without having large-scale political instability if we\'re in a recession of normal length. If you\'re in a much longer-run downturn, then all bets are off."<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Political scientists have argued that the economic stasis triggered social churning that got expressed through protests on a variety of issues across the developing world. In Brazil, disaffected youth rallied against a minor bus-fare hike;<sup id="cite_ref-nytReport_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytReport-200">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> in Turkey, they agitated against the conversion of a park to a mall<sup id="cite_ref-guardianReport_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardianReport-201">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> and in Israel, they protested against high rents in Tel Aviv. In all these cases, the ostensible immediate cause of the protest was amplified by the underlying social suffering induced by the great recession.\n</p><p>In January 2009, the government leaders of Iceland were forced to call elections two years early after the people of Iceland staged mass protests and clashed with the police because of the government\'s handling of the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC1_198-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC1-198">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> Hundreds of thousands protested in France against President Sarkozy\'s economic policies.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> Prompted by the financial crisis in Latvia, the opposition and trade unions there organised a rally against the cabinet of premier Ivars Godmanis. The rally gathered some 10\xe2\x80\x9320 thousand people. In the evening the rally turned into a <a href="/wiki/2009_Riga_riot" title="2009 Riga riot">Riot</a>. The crowd moved to the building of the parliament and attempted to force their way into it, but were repelled by the state\'s police. In late February many Greeks took part in a massive general strike because of the economic situation and they shut down schools, airports, and many other services in Greece.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> Police and protesters  clashed in Lithuania where people protesting the economic conditions were shot with rubber bullets.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> Communists and others rallied in Moscow to protest the Russian government\'s economic plans.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In addition to various levels of unrest in Europe, Asian countries have also seen various degrees of protest.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> Protests have also occurred in China as demands from the west for exports have been dramatically reduced and unemployment has increased. Beyond these initial protests, the protest movement has grown and continued in 2011. In late 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Occupy_Wall_Street" title="Occupy Wall Street">Occupy Wall Street</a> protest took place in the United States, spawning several offshoots that came to be known as the <a href="/wiki/Occupy_movement" title="Occupy movement">Occupy movement</a>.\n</p><p>In 2012 the economic difficulties in Spain increased support for secession movements. In Catalonia, support for the <a href="/wiki/Catalan_separatism" class="mw-redirect" title="Catalan separatism">secession movement</a> exceeded. On September 11, a <a href="/wiki/2012_Catalan_independence_demonstration" title="2012 Catalan independence demonstration">pro-independence march</a> drew a crowd that police estimated at 1.5&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Policy_responses">Policy responses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Recession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Policy responses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/National_fiscal_policy_response_to_the_Great_Recession" title="National fiscal policy response to the Great Recession">National fiscal policy response to the Great Recession</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Keynesian_resurgence" title="2008\xe2\x80\x9309 Keynesian resurgence">2008\xe2\x80\x9309 Keynesian resurgence</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%9308" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial crisis of 2007\xe2\x80\x9308">financial phase of the crisis</a> led to emergency interventions in many national financial systems. As the crisis developed into genuine recession in many major economies, economic stimulus meant to revive economic growth became the most common policy tool. After having implemented rescue plans for the banking system, major developed and emerging countries announced plans to relieve their economies. In particular, economic stimulus plans were announced in <a href="/wiki/Chinese_economic_stimulus_program" title="Chinese economic stimulus program">China</a>, the <a href="/wiki/American_Recovery_and_Reinvestment_Act_of_2009" title="American Recovery and Reinvestment Act of 2009">United States</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/2008_European_Union_stimulus_plan" title="2008 European Union stimulus plan">European Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> In the final quarter of 2008, the financial crisis saw the <a href="/wiki/G-20_major_economies" class="mw-redirect" title="G-20 major economies">G-20 group of major economies</a> assume a new significance as a focus of economic and financial crisis management.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_policy_responses">United States policy responses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Recession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: United States policy responses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_States_policy_responses_to_the_Great_Recession" title="United States policy responses to the Great Recession">United States policy responses to the Great Recession</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:U.S._Federal_Reserve_-_Treasury_and_Mortgage-Backed_Securities_Held.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/U.S._Federal_Reserve_-_Treasury_and_Mortgage-Backed_Securities_Held.png/250px-U.S._Federal_Reserve_-_Treasury_and_Mortgage-Backed_Securities_Held.png" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/U.S._Federal_Reserve_-_Treasury_and_Mortgage-Backed_Securities_Held.png/375px-U.S._Federal_Reserve_-_Treasury_and_Mortgage-Backed_Securities_Held.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/U.S._Federal_Reserve_-_Treasury_and_Mortgage-Backed_Securities_Held.png/500px-U.S._Federal_Reserve_-_Treasury_and_Mortgage-Backed_Securities_Held.png 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="720" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:U.S._Federal_Reserve_-_Treasury_and_Mortgage-Backed_Securities_Held.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Federal Reserve Holdings of Treasury and Mortgage-Backed Securities</div></div></div>\n<p>The Federal Reserve, Treasury, and Securities and Exchange Commission took several steps on September 19, 2008 to intervene in the crisis. To stop the potential run on money market mutual funds, the Treasury also announced on September 19, 2008 a new $50 billion program to insure the investments, similar to the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Deposit_Insurance_Corporation" title="Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation">Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation</a> (FDIC) program.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> Part of the announcements included temporary exceptions to section 23A and 23B (Regulation W), allowing financial groups to more easily share funds within their group. The exceptions would expire on January 30, 2009, unless extended by the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Reserve_Board" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Reserve Board">Federal Reserve Board</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Securities and Exchange Commission announced termination of short-selling of 799 financial stocks, as well as action against <a href="/wiki/Naked_short_selling" title="Naked short selling">naked short selling</a>, as part of its reaction to the mortgage crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> In May 2013 as the stock market was hitting record highs and the housing and employment markets were improving slightly<sup id="cite_ref-NYT52313_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT52313-213">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> the prospect of the Federal Reserve beginning to decrease its economic stimulus activities began to enter the projections of investment analysts and affected global markets.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-214">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia-Pacific_policy_responses">Asia-Pacific policy responses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Recession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Asia-Pacific policy responses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On September 15, 2008, China cut its interest rate for the first time since 2002. Indonesia reduced its overnight rate, at which commercial banks can borrow overnight funds from the central bank, by two percentage points to 10.25 percent. The <a href="/wiki/Reserve_Bank_of_Australia" title="Reserve Bank of Australia">Reserve Bank of Australia</a> injected nearly $1.5 billion into the banking system, nearly three times as much as the market\'s estimated requirement. The <a href="/wiki/Reserve_Bank_of_India" title="Reserve Bank of India">Reserve Bank of India</a> added almost $1.32 billion, through a refinance operation, its biggest in at least a month.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On November 9, 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_economic_stimulus_program" title="Chinese economic stimulus program">Chinese economic stimulus program</a>, a RMB\xc2\xa5 4 trillion ($586 billion) stimulus package, was announced by the central government of the People\'s Republic of China in its biggest move to stop the global financial crisis from hitting the world\'s second largest economy. A statement on the government\'s website said the State Council had approved a plan to invest 4 trillion yuan ($586 billion) in infrastructure and social welfare by the end of 2010. The stimulus package was invested in key areas such as housing, rural infrastructure, transportation, health and education, environment, industry, disaster rebuilding, income-building, tax cuts, and finance.\n</p><p>China\'s export driven economy is starting to feel the impact of the economic slowdown in the United States and Europe, and the government has already cut key interest rates three times in less than two months in a bid to spur economic expansion. On November 28, 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Finance_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Ministry of Finance of the People&#39;s Republic of China">Ministry of Finance of the People\'s Republic of China</a> and the <a href="/wiki/State_Administration_of_Taxation" title="State Administration of Taxation">State Administration of Taxation</a> jointly announced a rise in export tax rebate rates on some labour-intensive goods. These additional tax rebates will take place on December 1, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The stimulus package was welcomed by world leaders and analysts as larger than expected and a sign that by boosting its own economy, China is helping to stabilise the global economy. News of the announcement of the stimulus package sent markets up across the world. However, <a href="/wiki/Marc_Faber" title="Marc Faber">Marc Faber</a> claimed that he thought China was still in recession on January 16.\n</p><p>In Taiwan, the central bank on September 16, 2008, said it would cut its required reserve ratios for the first time in eight years. The central bank added $3.59 billion into the foreign-currency interbank market the same day. Bank of Japan pumped $29.3 billion into the financial system on September 17, 2008, and the Reserve Bank of Australia added $3.45 billion the same day.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Banks_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Banks-217">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In developing and emerging economies, responses to the global crisis mainly consisted in low-rates monetary policy (Asia and the Middle East mainly) coupled with the depreciation of the currency against the dollar. There were also stimulus plans in some Asian countries, in the Middle East and in Argentina. In Asia, plans generally amounted to 1 to 3% of GDP, with the notable exception of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_economic_stimulus_plan" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese economic stimulus plan">China</a>, which announced a plan accounting for 16% of GDP (6% of GDP per year).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_policy_responses">European policy responses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Recession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: European policy responses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Until September 2008, European policy measures were limited to a small number of countries (Spain and Italy). In both countries, the measures were dedicated to households (tax rebates) reform of the taxation system to support specific sectors such as housing. The European Commission proposed a <a href="/wiki/2008_European_Union_stimulus_plan" title="2008 European Union stimulus plan">\xe2\x82\xac200 billion stimulus plan</a> to be implemented at the European level by the countries. At the beginning of 2009, the UK and Spain completed their initial plans, while Germany announced a new plan.\n</p><p>On September 29, 2008, the Belgian, Luxembourg and Dutch authorities partially nationalised <a href="/wiki/Fortis_(finance)" title="Fortis (finance)">Fortis</a>. The German government bailed out <a href="/wiki/Hypo_Real_Estate" title="Hypo Real Estate">Hypo Real Estate</a>.\n</p><p>On October 8, 2008, the British Government announced a <a href="/wiki/2008_United_Kingdom_bank_rescue_package" title="2008 United Kingdom bank rescue package">bank rescue package</a> of around \xc2\xa3500 billion<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> ($850 billion at the time). The plan comprises three parts. The first \xc2\xa3200 billion would be made in regard to the banks in liquidity stack. The second part will consist of the state government increasing the capital market within the banks. Along with this, \xc2\xa350&#160;billion will be made available if the banks needed it, finally the government will write off any eligible lending between the British banks with a limit to \xc2\xa3250 billion.\n</p><p>In early December 2008, German Finance Minister <a href="/wiki/Peer_Steinbr%C3%BCck" title="Peer Steinbr\xc3\xbcck">Peer Steinbr\xc3\xbcck</a> indicated a lack of belief in a "Great Rescue Plan" and reluctance to spend more money addressing the crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> In March 2009, The European Union Presidency confirmed that the EU was at the time strongly resisting the US pressure to increase European budget deficits.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From 2010, the United Kingdom began a fiscal consolidation program to reduce debt and deficit levels while at the same time stimulating economic recovery.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> Other European countries also began fiscal consolidation with similar aims.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_responses">Global responses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Recession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Global responses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UK_US_2008_October_bank_bailouts.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/UK_US_2008_October_bank_bailouts.svg/350px-UK_US_2008_October_bank_bailouts.svg.png" width="350" height="311" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/UK_US_2008_October_bank_bailouts.svg/525px-UK_US_2008_October_bank_bailouts.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/UK_US_2008_October_bank_bailouts.svg/700px-UK_US_2008_October_bank_bailouts.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1441" data-file-height="1281" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UK_US_2008_October_bank_bailouts.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bank bailouts <a href="/wiki/2008_United_Kingdom_bank_rescue_package" title="2008 United Kingdom bank rescue package">in the United Kingdom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Troubled_Asset_Relief_Program" title="Troubled Asset Relief Program">in the United States</a> in proportion to their GDPs.</div></div></div>\n<p>Most political responses to the economic and financial crisis has been taken, as seen above, by individual nations. Some coordination took place at the European level, but the need to cooperate at the global level has led leaders to activate the <a href="/wiki/G-20_major_economies" class="mw-redirect" title="G-20 major economies">G-20 major economies</a> entity. A first summit dedicated to the crisis took place, at the Heads of state level in November 2008 (<a href="/wiki/2008_G-20_Washington_summit" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 G-20 Washington summit">2008 G-20 Washington summit</a>).\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/G-20_major_economies" class="mw-redirect" title="G-20 major economies">G-20 countries</a> met in a summit held on <a href="/wiki/2008_G-20_Washington_summit" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 G-20 Washington summit">November 2008 in Washington</a> to address the economic crisis. Apart from proposals on international financial regulation, they pledged to take measures to support their economy and to coordinate them, and refused any resort to protectionism.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/2009_G-20_London_Summit" class="mw-redirect" title="2009 G-20 London Summit">Another G-20 summit</a> was held in London on April 2009. Finance ministers and central banks leaders of the G-20 met in <a href="/wiki/Horsham" title="Horsham">Horsham</a>, England, on March to prepare the summit, and pledged to restore global growth as soon as possible. They decided to coordinate their actions and to stimulate demand and employment. They also pledged to fight against all forms of <a href="/wiki/Protectionism" title="Protectionism">protectionism</a> and to maintain trade and foreign investments. These actions will cost $1.1tn.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>They also committed to maintain the supply of credit by providing more liquidity and recapitalising the banking system, and to implement rapidly the stimulus plans. As for central bankers, they pledged to maintain low-rates policies as long as necessary. Finally, the leaders decided to help emerging and developing countries, through a strengthening of the IMF.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Policy_recommendations">Policy recommendations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Recession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Policy recommendations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="IMF_recommendation">IMF recommendation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Recession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: IMF recommendation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The IMF stated in September 2010 that the financial crisis would not end without a major decrease in unemployment as hundreds of millions of people were unemployed worldwide. The IMF urged governments to expand social safety nets and to generate job creation even as they are under pressure to cut spending. The IMF also encouraged governments to invest in skills training for the unemployed and even governments of countries, similar to that of Greece, with major debt risk to first focus on long-term economic recovery by creating jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Raising_interest_rates">Raising interest rates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Recession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Raising interest rates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Israel" title="Bank of Israel">Bank of Israel</a> was the first to raise interest rates after the global recession began.<sup id="cite_ref-marketwatch.com_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marketwatch.com-225">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> It increased rates in August 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-marketwatch.com_225-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marketwatch.com-225">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On October 6, 2009, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> became the first G20 country to raise its main interest rate, with the <a href="/wiki/Reserve_Bank_of_Australia" title="Reserve Bank of Australia">Reserve Bank of Australia</a> moving rates up from 3.00% to 3.25%.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Norges_Bank" title="Norges Bank">Norges Bank</a> of <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Reserve_Bank_of_India" title="Reserve Bank of India">Reserve Bank of India</a> raised interest rates in March 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes.com_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes.com-227">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On November 2, 2017 the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_England" title="Bank of England">Bank of England</a> raised interest rates for the first time since March 2009 from 0.25% to 0.5% in an attempt to curb inflation.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Comparisons_with_the_Great_Depression">Comparisons with the Great Depression</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Recession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Comparisons with the Great Depression">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Comparisons_between_the_Great_Recession_and_the_Great_Depression" title="Comparisons between the Great Recession and the Great Depression">Comparisons between the Great Recession and the Great Depression</a></div>\n<p>On April 17, 2009, the then head of the IMF <a href="/wiki/Dominique_Strauss-Kahn" title="Dominique Strauss-Kahn">Dominique Strauss-Kahn</a> said that there was a chance that certain countries may not implement the proper policies to avoid feedback mechanisms that could eventually turn the recession into a depression. "The free-fall in the global economy may be starting to abate, with a recovery emerging in 2010, but this depends crucially on the right policies being adopted today." The IMF pointed out that unlike the Great Depression, this recession was synchronised by global integration of markets. Such synchronized recessions were explained to last longer than typical economic downturns and have slower recoveries.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Olivier_Blanchard" title="Olivier Blanchard">Olivier Blanchard</a>, IMF Chief Economist, stated that the percentage of workers laid off for long stints has been rising with each downturn for decades but the figures have surged this time. "Long-term unemployment is alarmingly high: in the United States, half the unemployed have been out of work for over six months, something we have not seen since the Great Depression." The IMF also stated that a link between rising inequality within Western economies and deflating demand may exist. The last time that the wealth gap reached such skewed extremes was in 1928\xe2\x80\x931929.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Recession&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">\n<li style="display:table-row"><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/File:Emblem-money.svg" class="image"><img alt="icon" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Emblem-money.svg/28px-Emblem-money.svg.png" width="28" height="28" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Emblem-money.svg/42px-Emblem-money.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Emblem-money.svg/56px-Emblem-money.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48" /></a></span><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em
